  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ab18c60e-7e6b-4e23-9759-9959abb0a256'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText6116955843258540076" style="display:none">Tommy and Ozzie have been best friends since second grade, and boyfriends since eighth. They spent countless days dreaming of escaping their small town—and then Tommy vanished.<br /><br />More accurately, he ceased to exist, erased from the minds and memories of everyone who knew him. Everyone except Ozzie.<br /><br />Ozzie doesn’t know how to navigate life without Tommy, and soon suspects that something else is going on: that the universe is shrinking.<br /><br />When Ozzie is paired up with new student Calvin on a physics project, he begins to wonder if Calvin could somehow be involved. But the more time they spend together, the harder it is for him to deny the feelings developing between them, even if he still loves Tommy.<br /><br />But Ozzie knows there isn’t much time left to find Tommy–that once the door closes, it can’t be opened again. And he’s determined to keep it open as long as possible.</span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/22343742-jennifer-gosley"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1377699643i/22343742._UX100_CR0,8,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/22343742-jennifer-gosley">Jennifer Gosley</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    SPOILER...SPOILER.... Do NOT read this if you do not want to know events that happen throughout the book INCLUDING the ending. You've been WARNED!<br /><br />Your<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    SPOILER...SPOILER.... Do NOT read this if you do not want to know events that happen throughout the book INCLUDING the ending. You've been WARNED!<br /><br />Your question made me think about my take on the whole book. I feel that Tommy breaking up with Ozzie was just too much for his mind to handle. He couldn't imagine a world where he and Tommy weren't together, so his brain tried to help him through it by giving him a world where he would have no choice but to survive without Tommy and the time needed to accept the new reality ... also including a mechanism to get him back to his real life. Since the major events from the alternate timeline (like Warren's accident, roller coaster project, mom taking job in Chicago, etc.) also occurred in the original one, I think he may have been suffering from disssociative identity disorder. I've read that there can be alters that live parallel lives with the original personality. While the original Ozzie was working through the disappearance of Tommy, an alter was proceeding through his original life events. The universe shrinking was a timer for Ozzie and the alter to converge back to one whole person. The result was an Ozzie who could move past the breakup and flourish without Tommy. I know the belief that we must be strong on our own is probably why the author choose not to have Ozzie end up with Tommy or Calvin, but the romantic in me hopes that he eventually ends up with one of them (I'm leaning towards Calvin. I would love to ride the roller coasters that those two would design). :-)<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1906991385" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1906991385" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1906991385?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1906991385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10008803062865266241">Did you ever get the feeling you and an author would be great friends (or perhaps mortal enemies), simply based on the books they write and the way they tell stories? Even if that's irrational as thinking you'd be great friends with a television character, I still believe that from time to time.<br/><br/>Near the top of my list would be Shaun David Hutchinson, who absolutely slayed me with <b>
  <i>We Are the Ants</i>
</b> (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1623981314?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>see my original review</a>), which was in the top five of <a href='http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2017/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2016.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>the best books I read last year</a>. Now he's </span>
  <span id="freeText10008803062865266241" style="display:none">Did you ever get the feeling you and an author would be great friends (or perhaps mortal enemies), simply based on the books they write and the way they tell stories? Even if that's irrational as thinking you'd be great friends with a television character, I still believe that from time to time.<br /><br />Near the top of my list would be Shaun David Hutchinson, who absolutely slayed me with <b>
  <i>We Are the Ants</i>
</b> (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1623981314?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">see my original review</a>), which was in the top five of <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2017/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2016.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">the best books I read last year</a>. Now he's back with <b>
  <i>At the Edge of the Universe</i>
</b>, which I loved nearly as much, and it just convinced me I'd love to spend time just talking to Hutchinson and understanding how he thinks. At the very least, I'd love to be friends with one of his characters.<br /><br />Ozzie and Tommy have been best friends since childhood, and they've been boyfriends since the eighth grade. Tommy is so much of Ozzie's world, the two have weathered so much, particularly Tommy's abusive father, and they dream of one day escaping their Florida hometown. And then one day, Tommy disappears, without any warning. But worse that that, Tommy has ceased to exist—no one but Ozzie remembers Tommy, and all of the memories that the two shared, or shared with others, have been amended or totally rewritten.<br /><br />"It's impossible to let go of the people we love. Pieces of them remain embedded inside of us like shrapnel. Every breath causes these fragments to burrow through our muscles, nearer to our hearts. And we think the pain will kill us, but it won't. Eventually, scar tissue forms around those twisted splinters like cocoons. They remain part of us, but slowly hurt less. At least, I hoped they would."<br /><br />As Ozzie desperately tries to figure out what happened to Tommy, and convince those around him—including Tommy's mother—that he actually existed, Ozzie begins to realize that the universe is shrinking, and perhaps Tommy was taken away into some alternate universe. But that's not the only crisis Ozzie has to face—his parents are getting divorced, his older brother has joined the military and is about to head to basic training, and one of his best friends, Lua, is becoming distant as her dreams of musical success start coming to fruition.<br /><br />Then Ozzie is paired with Calvin on a physics class project. Calvin was once a star wrestler, class president, and all-around popular guy, until the day he quit wrestling and student council, came into school every day wearing the same hoodie and jeans, and mostly sleeps through class. Obviously there's something that made Calvin change so abruptly, and Ozzie wants to get to the bottom of it, but at the same time, he really can only focus on finding Tommy. But as he gets to know Calvin, he can't deny that he might be falling for him, but he doesn't know what to do—is it unfair to Tommy for Ozzie to pursue another relationship, or should he try and move on? And what if Tommy really doesn't exist?<br /><br />As the universe continues to shrink, and Ozzie's life continues to change, he knows he has a finite amount of time to find Tommy. But he also realizes there are so many more people in his life with problems. Should he help solve those, even if it might betray their trust, or should he not lose site of his goal? And will there be a universe left when he decides?<br /><br />Even though it's a little confusing when the plot goes all science-y, this is a beautiful book that hits you right in your heart. Once again, Hutchinson combines sci-fi and emotion to create a tremendously compelling, moving story about friendship, love, loyalty, trust, family, secrets, and selfishness. There is so much here to like, even if the characters aren't always 100 percent sympathetic, but it is Hutchinson's storytelling, his use of language and dialogue, that kicks this book up another notch. His characters may be wiser than their years, but they don't sound as if they just walked out of a John Green novel, where every sentence is a sarcastic burn or a philosophical insight.<br /><br />Hutchinson is open that as a teenager he struggled with depression and contemplated suicide, so he has a tremendous amount of empathy for his characters and their problems. I do wish he had dwelled a little less on the physics, but it didn't keep me from loving this book and these characters. Like <b>
  <i>We Are the Ants</i>
</b>, it will be a long while before I'll be able to get this story out of my mind. Is it 100 percent plausible? No. Does it matter? Not to me, given how tightly it grabbed my heart.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com">http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blo...</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10008803062865266241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2411329711?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481449670" href="/book/show/35297559-at-the-edge-of-the-universe">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2411329711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2723828859964493904">okay. lets get right to the point. this book was depressing. like, borderline adam silvera levels of sadness. but real life can sometimes be pretty woeful, so if there is anything this book was, it was real. the characters, the emotions, the struggles. they were so realistic, so relatable. <br/><br/>i was also impressed with how well this book covered some very sensitive subjects and content. it was a bit much at times, but i think that just lends to the storys authenticity and realistic nature. <br/><br/>the only </span>
  <span id="freeText2723828859964493904" style="display:none">okay. lets get right to the point. this book was depressing. like, borderline adam silvera levels of sadness. but real life can sometimes be pretty woeful, so if there is anything this book was, it was real. the characters, the emotions, the struggles. they were so realistic, so relatable. <br /><br />i was also impressed with how well this book covered some very sensitive subjects and content. it was a bit much at times, but i think that just lends to the storys authenticity and realistic nature. <br /><br />the only critique i have is the ending. i understand the sci-fi aspect of the plot and its necessity in helping ozzie to realise some things, but the ending kind of felt… like a cop out? i dont claim to know anything about physics or quantum mechanics, but it just felt weak in my opinion.<br /><br />overall, it was a great story, despite how depressing it was. i think sometimes sadness is the most effective emotion for me when it comes understanding the meaning of a book. and i thought this story had a pretty great message.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>4.5 stars</i>
</b></span>

<div id="review_1900257728" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1900257728" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1900257728?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481449663" href="/book/show/30312819-at-the-edge-of-the-universe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1900257728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14613081092359999761"><i>
  <blockquote>“I didn’t even need to check my phone to know that the universe had shrunk again, and the stars had vanished.<br/>No. They hadn’t vanished. I’d given them away to someone who hadn’t deserved them, and I’d never get them back.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><b>trigger warnings in this book for:</b> rape, statutory rape, racism, child abuse, graphic violence, self-harm, drugs, homophobia, ableism<br/><br/>I don't think its <b>any secret</b> I was a massive fan of Shaun David Hutchinson's 2016 release, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23677341.We_Are_the_Ants' title='We Are the Ants by Shaun David Hutchinson' rel='nofollow noopener'>We Are the Ants</a>, so his newest release was high on</span>
  <span id="freeText14613081092359999761" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“I didn’t even need to check my phone to know that the universe had shrunk again, and the stars had vanished.<br>No. They hadn’t vanished. I’d given them away to someone who hadn’t deserved them, and I’d never get them back.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br><b>trigger warnings in this book for:</b> rape, statutory rape, racism, child abuse, graphic violence, self-harm, drugs, homophobia, ableism<br><br>I don't think its <b>any secret</b> I was a massive fan of Shaun David Hutchinson's 2016 release, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23677341.We_Are_the_Ants" title="We Are the Ants by Shaun David Hutchinson" rel="nofollow noopener">We Are the Ants</a>, so his newest release was high on my 2017 anticipated list.<br><br>Fans of We Are the Ants will definitely enjoy At the Edge of the Universe - it features some of the same aspects that drew me into We Are the Ants - an honest look at mental illness and living as a gay teenager, beautiful prose, a sci-fi twist and raw emotion. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499436542i/23232591.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499436542i/23232592.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(by <a href="www.rykesmeadow.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">rykesmeadow</a> on tumblr)<br><br>At the Edge of the Universe follows Oswald Pinkerton, aka as Ozzie - who's pretty sure the universe is shrinking. His evidence? The boy he was dating, Tommy, has disappeared from the memory of everyone who knew him, including Tommy's family. This book follows Ozzie as he tries to unravel the mystery behind Tommy's disappearance and try to outlast the universe as it quickly shrinks around him. <br><br>I found <b>At the Edge of the Universe</b> a much harder read then We Are the Ants - the issues and themes covered are definitely heavy and you can practically feel the weight the characters are bearing. It's very gritty reading, but I think the issues were dealt with very gracefully and carefully. The characters are incredibly complex, and very very flawed - but while their choices may not be the best in each circumstance, I like that it was clear they weren't endorsed out of text. I also liked there is genuine growth for these characters, and that despite the truly horrible circumstances these characters are enduring, the ending is relatively happy. <br><br>I really liked the diversity in this one ! Ozzie is gay, Tommy is gay and biracial (one white one black parent), Lua, Ozzie's best friend, is gender-fluid and they're referred to with differing pronouns throughout the story. Ozzie's other best friend Dustin is asexual and Chinese-American, and another character Calvin is bisexual. I <b>loved</b> the amount of diversity in this story, especially Lua as a gender-fluid character because it is the first representation of gender-fluidity I've encountered personally. <br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“The funny thing is,' Calvin said, 'I thought I'd been breathing underwater this whole time, but I guess I've been drowning.”</blockquote>
</i><br><br>My main issues with this book is the ending, and the beginning. It took me a while to get into this, with the beginning being a little meandering and slow-paced. It took a while for me to figure out in what direction the book was going. I also wasn't the biggest fan of the final act, I don't think I really "got" the ending and I felt a little unsatisfied with some of the ending. <br><br>I was also a little irked about the ableism in this book - a character who cannot walk is referred to as "broken" and laments how no one will ever love him or want to be with him when he is a paraplegic. This was never challenged, and in the end there was a kind of "cure-all" for his situation. <br><br>Despite this, I really enjoyed the main content of this story. The story is definitely gritty, and there are bits and pieces I really felt horror reading - but I also think these issues were written and dealt with <b>so well</b>. This is ownvoices for mental illness and gay rep and I think it's important to tell our stories as marginalised people - both the good <i>and the bad</i>.<br><br>The prose, as expected, is beautiful. Shaun David Hutchinson has a very poetic and lyrical style, but it's very simple and not bogged down in overly flowery writing. I genuinely enjoy his writing so much. I also loved that Henry and Diego from We Are the Ants had a little cameo!<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“It's impossible to let go of the people we love. Pieces of them remain embedded inside of us like shrapnel. Every breath causes those fragments to burrow through our muscles, nearer to our hearts. And we think the pain will kill us, but it won't. Eventually, scar tissue forms around those twisted splinters like cocoons. They remain part of us, but slowly hurt less. At least, I hoped they would.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br>Shaun David Hutchinson has earned a spot on my instant buy list. At the Edge of the Universe is written with the same raw emotion, quirkiness and hard grit that made me fall in love with his stories. He constantly presents his readers with flawed, complex characters who must exist in incredibly difficult, but honest situations. <br><br>I love his books, and while this one didn't blow me away as much as We Are the Ants did, it's still a beautiful book. It' brutal and hard in places, but I think it is always honest and the narrative is layered I love Hutchinson's brand of sci-fi contemporary, and if you have enjoyed his previous books there will definitely be something for you here. If you haven't picked up one yet, I implore you too. At the Edge of the Universe would be a good place to start. <br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“Don't get so focused on where you're going that you forget the people you're travelling with. There's no point reaching a destination if you arrive alone.” </blockquote>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14613081092359999761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2395820857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1850682282981633577"><i>"We have to fall in love with the idea of a person before we can fall in love with the actual person."</i><br/><br/>Shaun's books have a safe place in my bookish heart. I love his characters, his stories, his style of writing. His books are unlike any other book I've read before and this one was no exception. The universe is shrinking and Ozzy's boyfriend Tommy has but nobody remembers that he existed. Only Ozzy does but, of course, no one believes him.<br/><br/>There are so many things that Shaun gets right. He is in </span>
  <span id="freeText1850682282981633577" style="display:none"><i>"We have to fall in love with the idea of a person before we can fall in love with the actual person."</i><br /><br />Shaun's books have a safe place in my bookish heart. I love his characters, his stories, his style of writing. His books are unlike any other book I've read before and this one was no exception. The universe is shrinking and Ozzy's boyfriend Tommy has but nobody remembers that he existed. Only Ozzy does but, of course, no one believes him.<br /><br />There are so many things that Shaun gets right. He is in touch with the young adult book community, he is aware of what occupies our minds and hearts, he listens. Which is why we get diversity and representation in the form of gay, genderfluid, bi- and asexual characters - or characters that don't know how or if to define themselves. But what might be even more important is that these characters have depth; they are relatable and not simply mere caricatures of what they represent. This is why OwnVoices authors are so important.<br /><br />What is even better, Shaun uses his books to talk about things that matter. He openly discusses depression, self-harm and how important it is to talk when one is hurting. He shows that love is not always easy and fluffy and relationships grow and change and always take two people who care enough to work on this relationship together. He does not shy away from topics like rape, abuse and poverty. I think it's brave that Shaun puts these stories out there and lends his ear and shoulder to so many kids, teens and adults. He makes them feel understood and seen and I think that is what every young adult author should set out to do.<br />I know that I'm seriously gushing about the author at this point but there is one more thing that I have to point out: this book features sex. It's explicit. That alone is still super rare in the YA genre. But here we have two gay teenagers who sleep with each other and it's not shown as something abnormal, it's not a taboo topic, it's what happens what two people have the hots for one another. I wish we could see more sex and more non-straight sex in young adult literature. Not because I read books for their erotic content, but because sex is how we all got here in the first place. <br /><br />Now the only thing I can criticise is related to the plot, so be aware of major spoilers. I shipped Ozzy and Calvin. I think I even fell for Calvin a little. So seeing his and Ozzy's relationship erased at the end of the book hurt. I understand that the story would not have worked otherwise, but I still rooted for them.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1850682282981633577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Cassandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22224742-cassandra"><img alt="Cassandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476890938p2/22224742.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1554246025?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cassandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cassandra" href="/user/show/22224742-cassandra">Cassandra</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22224742-cassandra?shelf=reads-of-2017">reads-of-2017</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1554246025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6841631344897518740">So instead of aliens trying to blow up the human homeland, the universe is now shrinking?<br/><br/>With most authors I'd be skeptical, but after We Are the Ants, Shaun David Hutchinson could write about rockette monkeys performing Chicago on Mars and I'd read it.<br/><br/><i>*After Actually Reading the Book*</i><br/><br/><i>
  <b> “Don’t get so focused on where you’re going that you forget the people yo’re travelling with. There’s no point reaching a destination if you arrive alone.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>After the god send known as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23677341.We_Are_the_Ants' title='We Are the Ants by Shaun David Hutchinson' rel='nofollow noopener'>We Are the Ants</a>, I was so </span>
  <span id="freeText6841631344897518740" style="display:none">So instead of aliens trying to blow up the human homeland, the universe is now shrinking?<br /><br />With most authors I'd be skeptical, but after We Are the Ants, Shaun David Hutchinson could write about rockette monkeys performing Chicago on Mars and I'd read it.<br /><br /><i>*After Actually Reading the Book*</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b> “Don’t get so focused on where you’re going that you forget the people yo’re travelling with. There’s no point reaching a destination if you arrive alone.”</b>
</i><br /><br />After the god send known as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23677341.We_Are_the_Ants" title="We Are the Ants by Shaun David Hutchinson" rel="nofollow noopener">We Are the Ants</a>, I was so excited for this book that I pre-ordered it four months in advance. Yep. I’m a slave to the writing of Shaun David Hutchinson. <br /><br />This book was even better than I hoped it would be. Plus, it had ties to both We Are the Ants and The Five Stages of Andrew Brawley (embed links). Diego and Henry (mainly Diego though) make an appearance, the Patient F movies are mentioned, and the main character of this novel, Ozzie, works at a book store and had to inform a customer that they don’t have a YA novel about ants and aliens. How both We Are the Ants is a book in this universe and Diego and Henry are spotted is beyond me, but I’m totally for it regardless. The more Diego the better, right?<br /><br />Ozzie is fantastic. He has a similar sense of humor as Henry, but Ozzie is completely his own man. When his boyfriend is suddenly erased from existence, Ozzie is willing to do anything to find him and bring him back. Even when his obsession begins to take its toll on his personal life. Then enter Calvin, his fellow student, who seems to have problems even deeper and more profound than Ozzie’s own. <br /><br />I’ll never not love these books. There’s something so unique and beautiful about them. Their oddball science fiction plotlines that somehow mix perfectly with extremely contemporary issues. Their broken and yet perfect boys. The sarcastic writing style that can’t be duplicated. I’ll recommend and love these books until my death bed. I swear on it.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“You can choose to be happy with what life gives you,” he said, “or spend your life miserable. I choose happiness. It’s really that simple.”</b>
</i></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1813649896" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1813649896" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1813649896?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481449663" href="/book/show/30312819-at-the-edge-of-the-universe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2017">y-out2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2019">z-read2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-specfic">sff-specfic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1813649896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12247629555480267463">This is a book about being human when the world around you is ending.<br/><br/>There is a lot I really liked about this book. Hutchinson is consistently good at making you feel the emotions of a piece, get caught up in the story: I was stressed and desperate to finish. I loved the strong prevalance of side characters. I think side character conflicts are an excellent addition to any book and are often sadly neglected. He’s also very good at dangling a mystery but giving it enough of a solid ending to be s</span>
  <span id="freeText12247629555480267463" style="display:none">This is a book about being human when the world around you is ending.<br /><br />There is a lot I really liked about this book. Hutchinson is consistently good at making you feel the emotions of a piece, get caught up in the story: I was stressed and desperate to finish. I loved the strong prevalance of side characters. I think side character conflicts are an excellent addition to any book and are often sadly neglected. He’s also very good at dangling a mystery but giving it enough of a solid ending to be satisfying: The ending of this book felt like exhaling. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>It used to bother me when I read books where the main characters fell in love or became best friends after only knowing each other a short time. I’d complained about it to Tommy once, and he’d said that’s how it happens in real life. Everyone we meet begins as a stranger, so we project onto them who we need them to be until we get to know them. He said we have to fall in love with the idea of the person before we can fall in love with the actual person.</i>
</blockquote><br />That being said, I feel like Hutchinson has fallen into a very clear formula, and this is just not as good an example of that formula. <i>We Are the Ants</i>, <i>The Five Stages of Andrew Brawley</i>, and to some degree <i>The Apocalypse of Elena Mendoza</i> all fall into a similar narrative: the apocalypse is threatened, the main character is depressed and generally not nice to other people, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and it turns out to be a metaphor for mental illness somehow <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I don’t think that’s actually a bad thing. It’s an interesting formula. It’s clearly working for him. I just think this book does very little with that formula compared to his others (especially <i>The Apocalypse of Elena Mendoza</i>). <br /><br />The middle of this could have been edited far better: this is a 500-page book, and I could <i>really</i> feel the lag around the middle. A lot of the middle is filled with side character conflict. I liked the blend of stories: Calvin’s story, specifically, was very good. I did not think most of these side characters had their arcs resolved in a meaningful way. <br /><br />Lua’s character arc, or rather lack of it, also somewhat bothered me. He’s meant to be flawed but likable, and at some points he comes off this way. Her other actions include: consistently blowing up at friends, telling Ozzie “you’re mine” in a conversation I thought was DEEPLY uncomfortable, and way more relevantly, throwing a glass bottle at a significant other (it’s implied this is not an anomalous event). If any of these were meaningfully criticized I would not be bothered but as it is, one of these characters is casually participating in domestic abuse. For lols. <br /><br />I think the ending of this bothered me on a few levels, honestly. Though some reviewer friends of mine who felt it was a cop-out, I like the actual ending fine: I just thought it came too quickly without enough buildup. In a book where almost all of the side character conflicts, especially Calvin's major conflict, were wrapped up very quickly as well, this left me wanting more.<br /><br />I do think Shaun David Hutchinson is a very talented author and very good at drawing readers into a story: I also like that he addresses topics from his past in such a good way. But this just isn't all that satisfying to me as a full narrative.<br /><br />TW for statutory rape, child abuse, domestic abuse. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://sptfy.com/4F6I" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://thebookishactress.carrd.co/#about" rel="nofollow noopener">About</a> |</span>
  <a data-text-id="12247629555480267463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15589481619634705345"><b>2 Stars</b><br/><br/><i>"It’s impossible to let go of the people we love. Pieces of them remain embedded inside of us like shrapnel. Every breath causes those fragments to burrow through our muscles, nearer to our hearts. And we think the pain will kill us, but it won’t. eventually scar tissue forms around those twisted splinters like cocoons. They remain part of us, bus slowly hurt less. At least, I hoped they would."</i><br/><br/>Ozzie’s boyfriend, Tommy disappeared two months ago. No one looking for him, not the police and</span>
  <span id="freeText15589481619634705345" style="display:none"><b>2 Stars</b><br /><br /><i>"It’s impossible to let go of the people we love. Pieces of them remain embedded inside of us like shrapnel. Every breath causes those fragments to burrow through our muscles, nearer to our hearts. And we think the pain will kill us, but it won’t. eventually scar tissue forms around those twisted splinters like cocoons. They remain part of us, bus slowly hurt less. At least, I hoped they would."</i><br /><br />Ozzie’s boyfriend, Tommy disappeared two months ago. No one looking for him, not the police and not even his parents. Ozzie is the only one who’s looking for him.<br /><br /><i>"I met Tommy in second grade. He kissed me in eighth. He was my boyfriend and best friend. July third, he was existed; July fourth he didn’t. not even his parents remember him."</i><br /><br />So to find Tommy, Ozzie is going to go to Seattle but when he was in the plane, the deputy takes him off the plane and then Ozzie watched his plane tumble from the sky and crash into boulevard. And when every one was shocked, he just laughed and laughed and… So yes the next scene was him with a therapist.<br /><br />Ozzie has a theory about "false vacuum" and he relates the plane incident and Tommy’s disappearance and shrinking the universe to this theory. If you’re wondering what’s this false vacuum theory you should read the story. So is the universe really shrinking? Is Ozzie’s theory correct? Most importantly, where is Tommy? If he’s real why does no one know anything about him?<br /><br />Well, I’m not a huge fan of Si-Fi but it’s good to read some of these books once in awhile for changing of the plot. So I read this book’s synopsis and it really intrigued me! The story started off really good and I thought wow it’s interesting but I lost interest the deeper I went into the story. And based on the ratings and the reviews I think it’s just me. Unfortunately, it didn’t work out for me. I didn’t enjoy it. I got bored and after the first half I skipped and skimmed a lot. Please remember, it was just my opinion so you can pay no attention to it and read it yourself. Hope you enjoy it!</span>

<div id="review_2279097736" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2279097736" />
    <a title="Silvia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13306676-silvia"><img alt="Silvia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572029941p2/13306676.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2279097736?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Silvia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Silvia " href="/user/show/13306676-silvia">Silvia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=rep-gay">rep-gay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=1st-person">1st-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=pride-recs">pride-recs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2279097736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11987426723804721851">This was my first book by SDH and I've been so hyped about his work that this could have easily gone the "it didn't live up to my expectations" way. But! It didn't! I have no idea what I expected from this in terms of plot and characters but I can say that <b>it was definitely worth the hype</b> (I say hype but how come only around 1800 people have rated this on goodreads?? How???)<br/><br/>Anyway, I don't have a copy of this anymore because I read it on Riveted, so this is a short review with no quotes or anyth</span>
  <span id="freeText11987426723804721851" style="display:none">This was my first book by SDH and I've been so hyped about his work that this could have easily gone the "it didn't live up to my expectations" way. But! It didn't! I have no idea what I expected from this in terms of plot and characters but I can say that <b>it was definitely worth the hype</b> (I say hype but how come only around 1800 people have rated this on goodreads?? How???)<br /><br />Anyway, I don't have a copy of this anymore because I read it on Riveted, so this is a short review with no quotes or anything, but you should definitely go read this book.<br /><br />So, Ozzie is the only one who remembers his boyfriend Tommy. Everyone's history has been modified to reflect a world where Tommy was never born, But Ozzie knows he hasn't just dreamed Tommy. Throughout the book we see some of the memories he shared with Tommy, but the main story takes place in the present, where Ozzie life moves on, more or less, without Tommy. His disappearance isn't the only weird thing that's happened. The universe is also shrinking, and again, only Ozzy seems to know.<br /><br />I found the premise so intriguing that I was hooked on that alone from the start, but then as we learn more about Ozzie, his old friends Lua and Dustin and his new friend Calvin, I couldn't stop reading. <br /><br />The book touches on <b>many difficult and dark themes</b> that are a reality for so many young adults, so keep that in mind and look at the trigger warnings at the of my review to know some of the themes that are in this book (but keep in mind I might have missed some).<br /><br />The cast is also very <b>diverse</b>with Ozzie being gay, Tommy being a black gay boy, Lua being genderfluid, Calving being questioning/bi, and Dustin being coded as ace (the author confirmed he is, but the word is not on page because Dustin doesn't say it, so I guess he's questioning at the time of the book). <br /><br />I really don't want to spoil anything so I'll just say that reading this was great and especially the countdown of the size of the universe made it <b>impossible to stop reading</b>, as well as the question of why everything was happening.<br /><br />I can only recommend everyone to read it and find out everything by yourself.<br /><br /><b>TWs:</b> self harm, depression, sexual assault, abuse.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11987426723804721851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2295157915" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2295157915" />
    <a title="Benjamin " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33085883-benjamin"><img alt="Benjamin " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603806189p2/33085883.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2295157915?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin " href="/user/show/33085883-benjamin">Benjamin </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481449663" href="/book/show/30312819-at-the-edge-of-the-universe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33085883-benjamin?shelf=lgbttiqa">lgbttiqa</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2295157915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer267343745531599044"><u>Full review posted!</u><br/>.<br/>.<br/>.<br/>.<br/><b>All my life, I have been living at the edge of the Universe. Unfortunately, it took 19 years and a book for me to realize.</b><br/><blockquote>
<i>“We've all got things about ourselves we hate and these dark places inside of us we're terrified to show people. We live in constant fear that someone is going to discover the rotting corpses we keep buried in those dark places, and that when they do, they'll despise us for them.”</i> </blockquote><br/>At The Edge of the Universe follows the story of Ozzie, a boy who is liv</span>
  <span id="freeText267343745531599044" style="display:none"><u>Full review posted!</u><br>.<br>.<br>.<br>.<br><b>All my life, I have been living at the edge of the Universe. Unfortunately, it took 19 years and a book for me to realize.</b><br><blockquote>
<i>“We've all got things about ourselves we hate and these dark places inside of us we're terrified to show people. We live in constant fear that someone is going to discover the rotting corpses we keep buried in those dark places, and that when they do, they'll despise us for them.”</i> </blockquote><br>At The Edge of the Universe follows the story of Ozzie, a boy who is living in a world in which nobody but him remembers his boyfriend Tommy ever existed. History has been rewritten, the universe is shrinking, and it seems as Ozzie’s duty to understand what’s happening so he can save the universe before it's too late. <br><br>If I had to astrophysically explain what this book is about, I couldn’t do it because I don’t know anything related astrophysics. However, I can tell you once you have finished this book your mind will be a cluster of emotions and crazy theories fighting against each other. <br><br>I know a book is good when it follows the Powerpuff Books’ formula: a wide range of representation, science, and humor. <br><br>The author has done an incredible job by catching the reader’s attention from the very first chapter to the last sentence of the book. Hutchison writing style is capable of stealing your soul so it can later get mixed with the story, and you can truly live each part of it. On the other side, even though there are some paragraphs explaining physic theories, they never became tedious or difficult to understand, as a matter of fact, they worked perfectly to disguise and transform the story’s meaning into something that left for the reader’s judgment. <br><br>Each character’s personality is so well developed, and they are all so unique that it results impossible not to love them all.<br><br><b>Ozzie’s</b> determination to prove his boyfriend’s existence and to find him while trying to help Calvin overcome his demons was so emotive that I even heard the sound ice breaking inside my chest. (If you are planning to read this book, I recommend you pay close attention to Ozzie’s attitudes). <br><blockquote>
  <i>“Sometimes I wish I'd find a zipper on the back of my head so I could unzip my skin and find the real me underneath.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>Calvin</b>, my sweet cinnamon roll, was for me the character with more personality, and the one who deserved more leadership than what was given to him. The message sent by the author through him made me remember how fragile and exposed we are as human beings and how our craving for feeling love can lead us to the wrong path. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1557933805i/27513451._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Lua</b> is the non-binary character we all needed in this book. They’re Ozzie’s best friend and a talented musician who are trying to find that sense of purpose in their life. If you ever wonder what true friendship is like, you will find it written in this book. I stan Lua for the rest of my life. <br><br>The themes the author approached through <b>Tommy</b>, the handsome and smart guy who makes the impossible became possible, are delicate and not always easy to write about. However, he managed to do it as well as he did with Calvin before. I wish with all my heart that David Hutchinson gets to write a story starring Tommy, I did not have enough. <br><br>David Hutchinson has created a fast-paced story, full of intrigue, memorable characters and life teachings that will make you want to lay on the floor and think on the vast existence of the universe and its future possibilities. <br><br>P.S: I’m still trying to remember how it feels to have a heartbeat. <br><br>(I even made a playlist for those who want to check it out <a href="https://open.spotify.com/user/arth%C3%BBro/playlist/5dgvmkpYcrONIFl4DFw0u8?si=EZZmu47TQ8y6jR-jEcG7EQ" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>).</span>
  <a data-text-id="267343745531599044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Maria (Big City Bookworm)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2567068-maria-big-city-bookworm"><img alt="Maria (Big City Bookworm)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558875339p2/2567068.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481449663" href="/book/show/30312819-at-the-edge-of-the-universe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2567068-maria-big-city-bookworm?shelf=2017-new-releases">2017-new-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2567068-maria-big-city-bookworm?shelf=on-my-shelf">on-my-shelf</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1671792490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3105729931544054045"><a href='https://bigcitybookworm.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455899354i/18166743.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></a><br/><br/>It definitely is no secret that At The Edge Of The Universe was probably my most anticipated book of the year. After reading We Are The Ants last year and completely falling in love with it, I was ready to read absolutely everything ever written by Shaun David Hutchinson.<br/><br/>--<br/><br/><b>What I Liked</b><br/><br/><b>The writing.</b> Shaun David Hutchinson just has this way of completely pulling you in with his writing. There’s just something so beautiful and magical about it. For those of you who know me, you know that my attentio</span>
  <span id="freeText3105729931544054045" style="display:none"><a href="https://bigcitybookworm.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455899354i/18166743.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>It definitely is no secret that At The Edge Of The Universe was probably my most anticipated book of the year. After reading We Are The Ants last year and completely falling in love with it, I was ready to read absolutely everything ever written by Shaun David Hutchinson.<br><br>--<br><br><b>What I Liked</b><br><br><b>The writing.</b> Shaun David Hutchinson just has this way of completely pulling you in with his writing. There’s just something so beautiful and magical about it. For those of you who know me, you know that my attention span is actual garbage, so for me to read 300 pages of a book in one sitting without any side distractions is an actual miracle and that is exactly what happened to me while reading At The Edge Of The Universe. I honestly didn’t even realize I read that much until I was finally able to put it down thanks to jet lag and fatigue.<br><br><b>The characters.</b> Along with writing a beautiful story, Shaun David Hutchinson continues to write beautiful characters. Every single one of them is perfect. Whether it’s the main characters, the side characters, the parents or even teachers…they are all wonderful to read. They are compelling and diverse and I just love every single one of them.<br><br><b>The shrinking universe.</b> Hutchinson seems to always find a way to add an almost magical realism element to his stories, whether it was the alien abductions in We Are The Ants or the shrinking universe in At The Edge of the Universe. These elements are truly unique and add a little something extra to each story.<br><br>--<br><br><b>What I Didn’t Like</b><br><br><b>Too similar.</b> While I absolutely loved At The Edge Of The Universe, it felt a little too similar to We Are The Ants at times. There was a moment that hinted that these two books may possibly take place in the same universe and while I liked that aspect, I still felt like the line between the two stories almost blurred together at times.<br><br>--<br><br>Overall, At The Edge Of The Universe was everything I had hoped it would be. While it did feel a little similar to We Are The Ants at times, it was still so beautifully written and completely captivating. I honestly can’t wait to read what Shaun David Hutchinson comes out with next!<br><br>--<br><br><b>Initial post reading thoughts:</b><br><br>It's no secret that this has been my most anticipated read for a very long time now. I love literally everything that I have ever read by Shaun David Hutchinson and I couldn't wait to pick this novel up.<br><br>Shaun David Hutchinson has this way of just completely drawing me in with his writing. I honestly can't remember the last time I read over 300 pages in one sitting. I know that is maybe normal for some readers, but as you may know, I have the worst attention span of all time. It takes a lot for me to devote hours on end to reading a book without any breaks in between and At The Edge Of The Universe completely drew me in, the same way that We Are The Ants did.<br><br>That being said, We Are The Ants is still my number one. At times, At The Edge Of The Universe felt very similar to We Are The Ants, but not in a bad way...just as if they took place in the same Universe (haha). I still completely 100% enjoyed the hell out of this novel and I can't wait for what Shaun David Hutchinson releases next!</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1900262221?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Camille ☼" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Camille ☼" href="/user/show/25663885-camille">Camille ☼</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1900262221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11166993664052308743"><i>“Don't get so focused on where you're going that you forget the people you're travelling with. There's no point reaching a destination if you arrive alone.”</i><br/><br/><b>4.5</b>. I don’t even know what to say this book was incredibly painful and beautiful and <i>why has not more people read this already</i>. This is amazing. Shaun David Hutchinson is amazing. <br/><br/>I loved the main character Ozzie and I loved seeing the story develop around him, seeing him grew up and master his anxiety and his fears. He’s a deeply unperfect </span>
  <span id="freeText11166993664052308743" style="display:none"><i>“Don't get so focused on where you're going that you forget the people you're travelling with. There's no point reaching a destination if you arrive alone.”</i><br /><br /><b>4.5</b>. I don’t even know what to say this book was incredibly painful and beautiful and <i>why has not more people read this already</i>. This is amazing. Shaun David Hutchinson is amazing. <br /><br />I loved the main character Ozzie and I loved seeing the story develop around him, seeing him grew up and master his anxiety and his fears. He’s a deeply unperfect and relatable character and he has so much love to give. My heart broke for him and for the other characters. This book is full of representation and <b>diversity</b>. There is Lua, who refuses to be labelled as one gender, Dustin who is asexual and Calvin who is bisexual. There is talk of mental illness, depression, abuse and many other things. This book is painful. I swear this book isn’t ALL sadness but don’t go reading this thinking it will be all sunshine and bunnies. But go read it. <br /><br />I only withdrew half a star because the end disappointed me a little, I feel like I was expecting something else and like a lot of things were left unresolved. <br /><br />Oh and this : <i>“A couple of customers interrupted [...] who wanted to know if we had some YA book about ants and aliens I'd never heard of”</i>. I SEE WHAT YOU DID THERE. For fans of <i>We are the Ants</i> like me.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />---------------<br /><br />15/06/2017 - While I'm drowning in my tears because I had to order a copy of <i>Our Dark Duet</i> that won't arrive before at least a week, I thought a book from the author of <i>We are the Ants</i> could only be a good distraction. <br /><br />I'm actually super excited to read this.</span>

<div id="review_2284680076" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2284680076" />
    <a title="Jackie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34560596-jackie"><img alt="Jackie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507559982p2/34560596.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2284680076?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie" href="/user/show/34560596-jackie">Jackie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34560596-jackie?shelf=my-heart-hurts">my-heart-hurts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2284680076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6632847385882524600">JUST POSTED MY FULL REVIEW (this is a first omg y'all better appreciate my efforts)<br/><br/><b>this was my first book by shaun david hutchinson and holy shit, i wasn‘t ready.</b><br/><br/>i found myself being able to relate to the characters a lot (especially calvin) and reading this book was a very heavy and emotional experience for me because it dealt with things that i went/go through as well.<br/><br/>content warnings for <b>depression, self-harm, drugs, rape, domestic violence and child abuse.</b><br/><br/>i never expected to like or relate t</span>
  <span id="freeText6632847385882524600" style="display:none">JUST POSTED MY FULL REVIEW (this is a first omg y'all better appreciate my efforts)<br /><br /><b>this was my first book by shaun david hutchinson and holy shit, i wasn‘t ready.</b><br /><br />i found myself being able to relate to the characters a lot (especially calvin) and reading this book was a very heavy and emotional experience for me because it dealt with things that i went/go through as well.<br /><br />content warnings for <b>depression, self-harm, drugs, rape, domestic violence and child abuse.</b><br /><br />i never expected to like or relate to this book as much as i did. the author managed to <b>depict mental illness in such a raw and honest manner</b> and i don't think i've ever come across characters that i could relate to so much in terms of their emotions and views of themselves. i believe the author himself suffers from depression (<b>which makes this an #OWNVOICES book</b>) and it clearly showed in the realness of the characters.<br /><br />calvin is the one character that my heart was weeping for. he's already suffered through SO MUCH at such a young age and i'm so sad for him. <b>i could see myself in him in so many ways</b> especially when it came to his depression because we seem to have very similar coping and defense mechanisms and i just wanted to hug him and tell him it's all gonna be OKAY :(<br /><br /><b>this book very much focuses on the dark and negative sides of mental illness</b> which made it a very heavy and difficult read at times (i had to pause several times to take a breath and clear my head), but it doesn't make it any less important. <br /><br />yes, i love reading books where characters deal with their mental illness in a healthy way and it's good to have positive and hopeful endings that remind you not to succumb to your mental illness, that focus on moving forward... but it's just as important to show the negative sides. to make people realise that things might not always be all happy-sunshine-rainbowland. that things get bad. to force people to pay attention, to know the signs.<br /><br />i think shaun david hutcherson did a beautiful job with this story and i want to give him all the stars and awards.<br /><br />it's also worth noting that this book features a <b>genderfluid character</b> that goes by both he and she pronouns and an <b>asexual (side) character</b>. and don't forget the gay kids who apparently live in seperate universes now!<br /><br />the only thing i disliked about this book was the fact that <b>it took me a while to get into it because i didn't really know where the story was going</b>, but i ended up flying through it within two days (also because i read this on Riveted and TIME WAS RUNNING OUT)<br /><br />OH AND THE ENDING KINDA BOTHERS ME. WHYYYY. no spoilers but i'm so <i>unsatisfied</i>.<br /><br />btw is anyone else thinking of Even from Skam when looking at the cover?? i swear the guy is wearing the exact same outfit that Even used to wear in the show<br /><br />overall, i definitely enjoyed this book <i>a lot</i> and i think hutchinson is a brilliant writer. i'll definitely read more of his works (especially if they're as raw and honest and GAY as this one).</span>
